Local News

Mr. and Mrs. Kong Xiangxi 155

Reception for U.S. Congressional Delegation ▲Numerous Chinese and Foreign Socialites in Attendance ▲U.S. Congressional Delegation Departs Shanghai Today ▲Mr. Pittman to Return Home at the End of the Month

Mr. and Mrs. Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry, hosted a tea party yesterday afternoon from 4:00 PM to 6:00 PM at Chen Bingqian's residence at No. 6 West Seymour Road to receive the U.S. Congressional Delegation. Numerous Chinese and foreign socialites were in attendance. The garden was beautiful, with lush greenery. Regrettably, with the Yellow Plum season just beginning, the weather was unpredictable. Refreshments were set up in the East and West living rooms, and the guests and hosts chatted and laughed as if meeting old friends. Melodious music emanated from both corridors. U.S. Senators Oddie and Robinson, as well as Congressman Doutel and their families, were specially invited and escorted into the living room by personnel from the Ministry of Industry. They shook hands with the host, Mr. and Mrs. Kong, and exchanged pleasantries. Mr. Oddie then told this newspaper's reporter that Congressman Gibbon had been ill for several days and had gone aboard the USS Henderson to recuperate. He regretted that he was unable to participate in the grand gathering. He also said that he and Senator Pittman were in China to study the silver issue separately. Mr. Pittman is currently in Peiping and will return to Shanghai in a few days. He will release a report after returning to the United States. The four, including Mr. Oddie, are scheduled to depart Shanghai today aboard the USS Henderson, heading to Manila on their way back to the United States. In addition to the congressmen's families, there are also more than 100 key figures from the U.S. military and political circles, 170 U.S. sailors, and 358 sailors. As for Mr. Pittman, he will pass through Beijing from Peiping in the coming days and return to Shanghai. He will take another ship back to the United States around the 24th or 25th of this month. Regarding the prospects of the International Silver Conference, it is understood that the Chinese banking community finds the situation complex and has not yet made any concrete statements to the U.S. congressmen.

Yesterday, those who also attended Mr. Kong's tea party included U.S. Ambassador Johnson, Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun, newly appointed Ambassador to France Qian Xinzhi, U.S. Consul General Cunningham and his wife, British Consul General Brenan, Chief of Customs Maze, Chief of the Shanghai Municipal Police Chen Xizeng, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai, Chinese Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Hu Mengjia, President of St. John's University Bu Fangji, President of Jiaotong University Li Zhaohuan, President of Fudan University Li Denghui, General Secretary of the YMCA Chen Liting, Principal of St. John's Middle School Na Deng and his wife, President of the Bank of China Zhang Jia'ao, President of the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank Chen Guangfu, as well as Song Ziliang, Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Zhang Zhuping of this newspaper, Gu Angruo, Dong Xianguang of the Continental Daily News, and Powell of Millard's Review, totaling more than 100 people.

Shipping Guild 156

Please Revise the Maritime Law ▲ Remove Obligation to Remove Sunken Ships ▲ The Shanghai Shipping Guild yesterday submitted a petition to the Legislative Yuan, stating that it was petitioning for the revision of the articles of the Maritime Law regarding the obligation to remove sunken ships, and earnestly requesting review and implementation. Since the promulgation of the Maritime Law, various shipping companies, due to their close relationship, have conducted thorough research to avoid conflicts and to facilitate compliance. Although there are many aspects that are not entirely suitable for our country's shipping merchants, the most significant damage and unbearable burden for shipping merchants is Article 23, Section 6. Upon repeated requests from members, the guild has petitioned for revisions in the past. This was submitted to a special members' meeting for public discussion. It was unanimously agreed that our country's shipping industry is undeniably in its infancy and relies entirely on the government's principle of providing the utmost protection to offer treatment suitable to its level, in order to safeguard the existing and promote the future. Although there are many methods, the law is the most important. Now, because our country's maritime industry has no precedent to follow, the Maritime Law has been compiled and implemented to bring it onto the right track and achieve the rule of law. The intention is excellent. It is believed that the reason our government implemented tutelage before constitutional government was because it recognized that the people's overall level had not yet reached a sound state, so it lightened their burden, aiming to ensure it was within their capacity, guiding them gradually to seek suitability. Shipping merchants are one part of the people as a whole, and their level is also very elementary, with training just beginning. Responsibility should be slightly relaxed to allow for development and hope. In today's shipping industry, the essence of laws and regulations should naturally embody the intention to protect and support, to nurture the budding sprouts of existing businesses, and to stimulate the investment interest of those in the future, so that the number of Chinese ships increases daily. Once maritime rights are recovered and Chinese ships are sufficient to supplement them, the realization of doctrines will rely on this practicality. The relationship is extremely important. Examining maritime operations, they inherently contain danger, and shipwrecks are a common occurrence. Now, listing the removal of sunken ships as one of the responsibilities of shipowners seems to imply a punitive intent. However, when the causes of ship sinkings are investigated, whether they are self-inflicted or caused by collisions, they are generally not intentional. Since they are not intentional, there is no basis for punishment. To say it is a matter of holding someone responsible for their actions, there is even more to say. For example, if someone is driving a car on a main road and is hit and the car is destroyed, leaving it on the road would obstruct traffic. The local police authorities would naturally immediately remove it. One has never heard of the car owner being ordered to remove it themselves. This is because the car has already paid taxes, and the car owner is a taxpayer to the state or local area. The local police authorities' expenditure to remove it on their behalf is merely fulfilling their due obligations. Comparing maritime law to land law, comparing ships to cars, and comparing shipowners to car owners, the situations and positions are completely identical, and there is no possibility of ordering it. Moreover, in reality, the majority of shipping companies in our country own only one ship. The capital raised is often insufficient to cover the ship's value, so they borrow and mortgage to supplement it. The insurance amount is set at the standard of the loan mortgage amount due to saving expenses. Payment of the insurance amount requires a considerable amount of time. After obtaining it, it is often insufficient to repay the debt. They are already struggling to compensate for the remaining ship value and the various expenses of negotiation, compensation, and severance. Therefore, even if they are ordered to remove the sunken ship, it is impossible to make something out of nothing, and it cannot become a reality. Therefore, merely having laws without the ability to enforce them is not the government's original intention in legislating. Furthermore, some may refer to the insurance amount as the ship value, but it is not known that insurance is a contractual act, containing a preparatory nature, to meet the needs of replenishment and to aim for a day of recovery. Therefore, although insurance uses the ship as the subject matter, the intended use of the amount paid after the insurance is determined in advance, and it should not be regarded as the ship value. This is not a theoretical matter. In 1923, various countries convened the International Maritime Law Conference in Geneva and agreed on the uniform treaty for maritime disasters. Article 5 adopted a proactive approach to insurance claims, considering them as a reserve fund for shipowners to restore business and compensate for losses, and absolutely not recognizing them as ship value. This has become a common international practice. Furthermore, in terms of laws and regulations, when a ship sinks under the circumstances listed in Articles 163, 1, 2, and 3 of this law, the shipowner may declare abandonment. Once abandoned, their status as the owner is terminated, and as they are no longer the owner, they naturally do not bear the responsibility of contributing to the removal. Moreover, in the United Kingdom, which has advanced maritime commerce, the Sunken Vessels Act of 1877 and Articles 530 to 32 of the Merchant Shipping Act of 1894 assign the responsibility for removing sunken vessels to the port authority. The expenses are paid from the maritime fund, in addition to using the items salvaged from the sunken vessel to offset the cost. These laws and regulations are sufficient for our country to learn from. Moreover, various countries in the East and West promote shipping without empty talk, allocating huge amounts of money annually to provide practical subsidies. Although the methods vary, the key to protection and the thoroughness of cultivation are the same. All these facts are clearly understood. Our country's unification has just been completed, and the treasury has not yet been replenished. Although the government intends to imitate this, its strength is still limited. Shipping merchants humbly understand the difficult times and dare not have extravagant hopes. However, concerning the government's designated funds from shipping merchants for specific uses, abandoning them and still ordering shipping merchants to bear the burden, the treatment is as different as heaven and earth. This is also something that shipping merchants are unwilling to accept. The so-called designated funds from shipping merchants for specific uses are the tonnage dues collected by customs, which are levied on ships and used for dredging waterways. The payment of tonnage dues by shipping merchants already covers the expenses on waterways. Government agencies clearing obstacles on waterways are merely fulfilling their due duties and should not damage the national treasury. If we follow the provisions of our country's Maritime Law and list the removal of sunken ships as the responsibility of shipowners and attempt to handle it accordingly, it would be practically impossible due to the environment. If we treat it as mere paperwork, we are afraid of trampling on the law. If it is forcibly enforced, once a ship sinks, there will be no basis for replenishment or hope for recovery. Our country's shipping merchants will inevitably decrease daily due to accidents. Not only will future investors regard it as a dangerous path due to the thought of gambling everything, but existing businesses will also sell out and switch to other industries because of one fall making it difficult to recover. This is contrary to the government's main objective of recovering shipping rights and promoting the shipping industry. All of this is due to laws and regulations that have not examined the facts or suited the level. The survival or abolition of this article is a matter of life and death for shipping merchants, and they are determined to appeal as much as possible to seek survival. Fortunately, the laws and regulations are newly enacted, and their suitability is still being tested. Therefore, revision is a necessary stage, and petitioning is a civil right conferred upon them. The guild should submit petitions to the Legislative Yuan and relevant ministries, earnestly requesting prompt revision to be changed to handling by the port authority, and the expenses to be paid from the tonnage dues, so as to alleviate pain and support development. The shipping industry and shipping rights are deeply intertwined with interests. Approaching the presentation, we cannot help but await your urgent orders.

Difficulty in Collecting Fushun Coal Export Tax 157

▲Due to Unreasonable Protest from Japanese ▲ According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the issue of collecting export taxes on Fushun coal passing through Dalian will soon escalate. Deputy Ambassador Shigemitsu visited Finance Minister Song Ziwen and Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting on the 17th to protest in person. However, Song and Wang both sternly rejected the protest. Song stated that this was an appropriate and reasonable measure, and Wang also stated that this was China's tariff autonomy and that foreigners could not interfere. If Japan insisted on refusing to pay, they would not hesitate to submit it to international judicial arbitration, as China had sufficient justification in terms of tax treaties. Yesterday, after reading this news, the Xin Sheng News Agency reporter happened to meet a key figure in diplomatic circles and discussed the brief history of the mine and the reasons for the protest. It was said that the Fushun Coal Mine includes several areas such as Qianjinzhai, Dashan, Dongxiang, Yangbaobao, Laohutai, Wandawu, and Xintun Longfeng. Although the total amount of reserves cannot be accurately known, according to past measurements, it is estimated to be over 100 million tons. On average, it can produce more than 9,000 tons per day. When it was first established, it was purely Chinese-owned. Later, due to operational difficulties, it was jointly operated with the Russians. After the Russo-Japanese War, Japan forcibly occupied the mine, claiming it was Russian-owned, and has been doing so ever since. The coal produced there is of excellent quality, and none of the coal produced in various mines in Japan can compete with it. Therefore, the Japanese industrial sector relies heavily on the supply from this mine. Now that the National Government has imposed an export tax on it, the impact on the Japanese side is conceivable. However, the Japanese seized our country's mineral resources to meet their own country's needs, and now they do not want to pay the export tax on it. Moreover, this export tax is not levied solely on Japan. Why should Japan protest this matter alone? Therefore, commentators believe that this is likely an unreasonable demand from the Japanese diplomatic community.

Shanghai Shipping Merchants Oppose 158

Customs Collects Tonnage Dues on Deck Cargo ▲ The Jianghai Customs announced that from July 1st, all deck cargo loaded on Yangtze River ships must be subject to tonnage dues, with a tax of one mace of silver per ton. Various shipping companies in this city believe that deck cargo should not be taxed as an exception, and have specially requested the Shipping Guild to petition the Ministry of Finance to exempt this special tax. The main reasons are that customs has regulatory measures for the transportation of goods by ships, and insurance companies have restrictive conditions. Items such as fish and fresh fruit, due to their perishable nature, cannot be loaded into the cargo hold. Also, items such as cotton and cloth, due to their flammability, are easily jettisoned and must be placed on deck or in the ship's passages, not because the cargo hold is full. Moreover, tax calculation hinders ship schedules, and restricting loading hinders the flow of goods. It should be requested that this tonnage due be immediately cancelled by the customs to alleviate merchants' difficulties.

Negotiations on the National Products Market Case Today 161

▲ Directors and Staff of the Public Works Department Invited ▲ Municipal Government Instructs to Claim Losses According to Law ▲ The Chinese National Products United Market has been ordered to close by the Public Works Department and has been closed for ten days. The Municipal Government has protested to the Public Works Department yesterday, and ordered the market to claim compensation for losses according to law. The various situations yesterday are recorded as follows. ▲ Negotiations Today National Products Market Committee Chairman Zhang Zilian and Hong Yanbin Ren Jinpin received a request from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai yesterday, urging them to go to the meeting at 4:00 PM today (19th). It is reported that the Chamber of Commerce also invited Hua Xun Yu Qiaqing, Western Director Bairang, and staff from the Public Works Department Fire Department of the Public Works Department to discuss the next steps together.

▲ Municipal Government Instructions The Municipal Government issued instructions to the National Products Market yesterday, stating that both submissions have been received. The Public Works Department of the International Settlement abruptly ordered the closure of the market and sealed it off due to the issue of the attached amusement department's license. It had not requested permission from the court beforehand.

The rash execution was a fundamental error, not only hindering our country's legal rights but also violating the agreement of the Shanghai International Settlement Special Court. The Secretariat of this government has been instructed to send a letter to the Public Works Department of the International Settlement to lodge a serious protest. As for the losses suffered by the market, the market should directly claim compensation according to law. This instruction is hereby notified. ▲ Ministry of Industry Instructions The Ministry of Industry received a report from the Industrial and Commercial Visiting Bureau, dispatched personnel to investigate the truth of the National Products Market case, which was ordered to close by the Public Works Department, and the process of negotiation. It immediately consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for investigation and handling. The National Products Market received instructions from the Ministry yesterday, stating that the telegram has been received and the situation has been reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for investigation and handling on the 13th of this month. This instruction is hereby notified. ▲ Bureau of Social Affairs Instructions The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs dispatched personnel to thoroughly investigate the closure order of the National Products Market by the Public Works Department and reported the situation to the Municipal Government a few days ago. Instructions were issued to the National Products Market yesterday, stating that the submission has been received and the situation has been reported to the Municipal Government to forward it to the Public Works Department of the International Settlement for protest. Further instructions will be issued after receiving instructions. This instruction is hereby notified.

Money shops will be closed for the holiday tomorrow and will resume business as usual on the 21st. Chinese and foreign banks will also close due to the closure of money shops. However, the Customs and the Central Bank will operate as usual.

Public Works Department Collects Land Tax on "Fangdan" Land 163

▲ Taxpayers Association Sent Letter to the Bureau Yesterday Requesting Correction ▲ The Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Joint Settlement sent a letter to the Director of the Public Works Department yesterday, stating that according to a letter from Mr. Gu Deqi, he sold a piece of land measuring 1.7 fen (a Chinese unit of area) to the Shanghai Public Works Department on June 25, 1928. The land is located west of Muir Ming Road in the settlement, registered as No. 2289 in the Public Works Department's register. The land is connected to the ancestral "fangdan" land. When buying the 1.7 fen of land, the Public Works Department instructed him to sign a contract stipulating that the land tax must be paid for the "fangdan" land as well. He was forced to sign the contract at the time and was unaware of the implications. Now he understands that the Public Works Department has no right to collect taxes on "fangdan" land. The contract he signed with the Public Works Department, stipulating that the "fangdan" land must pay taxes to the Public Works Department, violates the charter and is legally invalid. Moreover, the Public Works Department's sale of the remaining 1.7 fen of land to him is merely an ordinary transaction and there is no reason to make tax payment a condition for the "fangdan" land. He is ignorant and does not know the correct interpretation of this matter, so he is writing to request instructions for compliance. Based on this, the Executive Committee decided that in the interest of caution, Li Bohan and Liu Hongyuan were assigned to investigate. Now, according to the report, the point of contention is whether the Public Works Department can collect taxes on "fangdan" land according to the Yangjingbang Land Regulations. According to the investigation, the Public Works Department has never collected taxes on "fangdan" land. This is evidenced by pages 132 and 319 of Volume 1 of Judge Feitang's report. As for Gu Deqi's case, the Public Works Department had him sign a sales contract with an attached condition that the buyer must acknowledge the seller's right to collect taxes on his "fangdan" land when buying 1.7 fen of land from the Public Works Department. In terms of private law, private contracts are absolutely valid. However, there is an exception for contracts that violate public interest or national sovereignty, which are legally invalid. Moreover, using tax payment as a condition for a sales contract seems unreasonable in terms of law and sentiment. Whether or not this is appropriate is up to you to decide. This matter was referred to the Standing Committee, which decided to send a letter to your bureau for review and request that you correct this error immediately. While this was being processed, another letter was received from Mr. Wang Anfu, stating that he has an ancestral land plot located on East-West Huade Road. In 1924, when he rebuilt his house, the Public Works Department ordered him to cede a few feet of land and compensated him with 3,000 yuan. The following year, the Public Works Department started collecting land tax from him. However, his inheritance is a "fangdan" rather than a "daoqie" (official land deed). He pays grain tax to the Shanghai Municipal Government every year. Now, the Public Works Department is collecting land tax from him again. Although he protested, the Public Works Department forced him to pay, and he had no power to resist, so he had to pay. Moreover, because the amount was small at the time, the land has now been revalued by the Public Works Department, and he is now required to pay nearly 200 yuan per year in land tax. It is unreasonable for him to pay tax with a "fangdan". He is writing to request your association to uphold justice and negotiate with the Public Works Department. This matter should also be handled together. Please investigate and correct this error immediately.

Public Works Department 164

Revises Procedures for Property Rental Assessment ▲ Establishes Valuation Committee ▲ According to the Public Works Department Gazette, the revised procedures for property rental assessment are as follows: the bureau has hired three experts from outside the settlement to form a Rental Assessment Committee with two members from the bureau. All disputes regarding rental assessment for the purpose of collecting police rates will be resolved by the committee. If taxpayers are dissatisfied with the rental assessment made by the bureau, they should notify the director of the bureau in writing within 30 days of receiving the assessment notice and submit it to the committee for review. If no notice is submitted after 30 days, the police rates must be paid according to the assessed value. Furthermore, if taxpayers are still dissatisfied with the review result of the Rental Assessment Committee, they should provide reasons in writing and notify the director of the bureau within 30 days of receiving the review result notice, and submit it to the Tax Rate Appeals Committee for review. Otherwise, the review result must be absolutely complied with.

Wu Jingxiong's Future Report 165

▲ To be Completed Within One Year ▲ The second part of Judge Feitang's report, advisor to the Public Works Department of the International Settlement, has been published. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency interviewed Mr. Wu Jingxiong, the newly appointed advisor to the Public Works Department, and asked for his opinion on the report. Mr. Wu said that he had just received the second part of the report yesterday and was currently reading it. Although the facts on which Judge Feitang's report is based are quite accurate, due to the different standpoints and the complexity of the situation in Shanghai, there may be omissions in its objective aspects, which is inevitable. He (Mr. Wu referring to himself) plans to prepare a report within one year to contribute to the Public Works Department. He has already started working on it, and the materials in Judge Feitang's report are also worth collecting. The reporter asked what would happen if Mr. Feitang's report contradicted his opinion. Mr. Wu said that fortunately, the Public Works Department regards this report as a reference only, and not as a policy guideline. Therefore, the report he drafts will also be for the Public Works Department to use as a reference for research. Mr. Wu then said that a certain tabloid reported today (i.e., yesterday) that he would resign from the presidency of the Supreme Court, which was a completely unfounded rumor. Since he has a contract with the Public Works Department, apart from legal affairs that can still be carried out without conflict, it is not convenient for him to break the contract to take on other positions for the time being.

Customs Recovers River Berths on the Huangpu River 166

The Jianghai Customs has recovered the river berths on the Huangpu River that were occupied by foreign ships and naval vessels. Berths No. 7 and No. 8 were used by the Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK). When the customs went to recover them, the Japanese initially refused to return them. After several negotiations, the matter has now been resolved. The two river berths have been recovered by the Jianghai Customs, but for the convenience of NYK's ship mooring, the berths have been leased to the company, with a fixed monthly rent collected by the customs.

Reform of Japanese Raw Silk Inspection 168

▲ Japanese Government Decides to Implement Quality Inspection on Exported Raw Silk from January Next Year ▲ Japan is the largest silk-producing country in the world, exporting 600,000 bales annually, worth more than 300 million Japanese yen at current market prices. Its development is largely due to the government's research and encouragement, and the people's efforts to promote it. According to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's Raw Silk Inspection Office, the Japanese government has been researching raw silk grading. After two meetings, Japanese and American opinions have gradually converged. Also, in view of the fact that the inspection methods adopted by export silk merchants are not uniform, it has been decided that from January next year, all Japanese exported raw silk must undergo quality inspection at the two national raw silk inspection offices in Yokohama and Kobe, and be graded. Then, buying and selling will be based on the inspection results of the inspection offices. It is reported that after this is implemented, various trade disputes in raw silk trading will be reduced, and the credibility will be increased, the benefits of silk manufacturers will also be protected, and the Japanese raw silk grading work will be implemented. This is a great help to the Japanese raw silk trade, and our country should pay attention to it.

The draft of the collision truth signed by Captain Jia Shi of the ship and the British captain is being translated into Chinese and should be published today. The Yu Da wheel is scheduled to sail to Yingkou this afternoon.

Destruction of the Minghe Steamer 173

▲All Crew Members Rescued and Returned to Shanghai ▲British Steamer "Maqin" Also Unable to Help

The Ningbo-Shaoxing Steamship Company's "Minghe" steamer was wrecked off the coast of Haishenwai. The crew has now been rescued and returned. The ship has been completely destroyed, with losses amounting to hundreds of thousands of dollars. The salvage vessel "Fengpu" returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday. Our reporter made a special trip to investigate and learned the details, which are recorded as follows and should not be taken lightly.

▲Ship Owner Reports the Accident

Mr. Andy Wilkinson, the owner of the "Minghe" steamer, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and submitted a report stating that after the "Minghe" was chartered by the Soviet Russian fleet, it arrived off the coast of Zhupanova in Kemchatke's Peacock Harbor on April 22nd to await barges to transport goods. At that time, the barometer on the ship fell, and they dared not drop anchor. Instead, they used nets to block the wind and release pressure. Unexpectedly, a heavy snowstorm struck at night, and the ship could not withstand it. It was hit by huge waves onto the sandy beach, and the hull was stuck and unable to move. They urgently telegraphed for help. The Soviet team in Sui sent a ship to lighter the goods. The steamer was repeatedly struck by tides and waves, gradually being pushed towards the beach. Now, after more than 40 days, it has been completely washed onto the sandy beach and sunk into the mud.

▲The Rescue Efforts of the Fengpu

Upon receiving the news, the Shanghai General Bureau immediately dispatched the "Fengpu" steamer, along with workers and technicians from the Sanbei Company's factory, to carry out the rescue. While in Japan, they also hired several divers to go to the site of the accident together. After investigation, Zhupanova was still seven days' sailing from Sui. When the "Fengpu" arrived, it was observed that the "Minghe" was one nautical mile away from the sea. At low tide, the entire ship was on the shore. The steamer could not approach, and sampans could not reach it. After inspection by workers and technicians, and divers entering the water, all stated that it was too far from the sea and there was no such long cable for towing. To attempt a rescue, the project would be huge, costing at least four to five hundred thousand dollars, requiring the seabed to be deepened to allow water to enter the ship. As a result, after requesting instructions from the Shanghai Bureau, it was decided to abandon the ship.

▲Rescued Crew Returns to Shanghai

Upon receiving a reply telegram from the General Bureau, the "Fengpu" steamer transferred the 49 employees of the "Minghe" steamer, from the shipowner down to the workers, onto the ship and rescued them back to Shanghai. Since it was decided to abandon the "Minghe," all detachable items inside the ship were unloaded one by one and transported onto the "Fengpu" and loaded together. However, the engine, machinery, etc., could not be removed and had to be destroyed in the ship. Yesterday, the "Fengpu" returned. When the crew arrived in Shanghai, the Bureau ordered them to temporarily stay in Shanghai to be reassigned to other ships. It is noted that the "Minghe" steamer had a load capacity of 2,400 tons and was currently valued at 400,000 dollars, but was only insured for 80,000 taels, so the loss must be over 300,000 dollars.

▲The "Maqin" Also Abandoned

The "Nanshan Maqin" of the Laisi Foreign Firm, which ran aground in the same area last year, was also the target of a rescue attempt. This time, when the "Fengpu" went to rescue the "Minghe," Mr. Maqin, the owner of Laisi, also brought 16 rescue workers and technicians on the same ship to tow the vessel. However, after inspecting it at Peacock Harbor, its situation was the same as the "Minghe," impossible to salvage. They had to abandon this ship as well. Mr. Maqin had already taken the "Fengpu" steamer, leading the rescue workers, back to Shanghai. The abandonment of these two ships will result in a total loss of 700,000 to 800,000 dollars, which is a great misfortune for the Shanghai shipping industry.

Navigation News from the Upper Yangtze 177

▲Dispute Over Shipping Rights on the Sichuan River

Due to foreign merchants seizing business, Chinese shipping companies have suspended operations. As reported by this newspaper, yesterday, the local steamship companies received a telegram from Yichang stating that since foreign merchant ships joined the shipping association and broke up the Chinese merchant alliance, a major dispute has arisen in the shipping and navigation industries in Sichuan. The most important issues are: Chinese merchants proposed reducing the number of ships to even out business, but this was opposed by British Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire. As a result, only five Chinese ships remained, while foreign ships numbered nearly thirty. Regarding the issue of ship schedules, it was agreed that the first to arrive would depart first, but this was broken by Nissin Kisen Kaisha. Furthermore, it was later proposed that all ships on the Sichuan River reduce their cargo by half to prevent large ships from monopolizing the market, but this was rejected by the Yujiang Company. Finally, the Sichuan Chamber of Commerce refused to accept the new price of six taels per piece for cotton yarn water transport, only recognizing four taels per piece. As a result, a major dispute has arisen between the shipping and navigation industries in the Sichuan River. So far, neither side is willing to yield, and there is no solution. ▲American Steamer Rescued from Danger

The No. 1 steamer of the Shanghai Jiejiang Company ran aground near Yichang, as reported by this newspaper. Yesterday, definite news was received that the ship had been towed out by a ship dispatched by Jiejiang Yichang. The hull was not severely damaged, and the cargo was undamaged.

Continued Allocation of Disaster Relief Funds for Rehe Chaoyang

Wind and Hail Disaster in Song County Awaiting Relief 179

The Chinese Red Cross Society recently received a telegram from Chairman Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Association, stating that the Society should be aware that magistrate Han Haitao and Relief Association Chairman Li Yuchun of Song County sent a telegram reporting that according to the Bao Wei Tuan Zong Li Yinting and Li Guanggong of Qiuhuo and Xiaohe, etc. in the county's Western District, on the evening of May 30th and 31st at 5 PM, wind and rain suddenly arrived, accompanied by thunder and lightning, and hailstones fell, as large as chicken eggs, lasting for two hours, accumulating to a thickness of more than a foot, extending approximately thirty miles east and west and eighty miles north and south, with no place spared. The autumn seedlings were completely destroyed, and the ripening wheat was also severely damaged. The villagers suffered greatly from this disaster and are in unspeakable pain. Please promptly inspect the area, etc. The society immediately sent personnel to conduct a detailed survey, which confirmed the reported situation. Please quickly provide relief, etc. The county has been plagued by natural disasters and banditry, and the people have reached the point of extreme suffering. Currently, they are trying their best to provide relief and call back the refugees. Unexpectedly, they suffered another hailstorm, with no hope for the autumn harvest. The situation is tragic, and urgent relief is needed. It is hoped that the central government and charitable organizations will consider that the people of the county have been in dire straits for a long time, and have suffered such a severe disaster, with no harvest and no food. They are imploring for quick relief and generous donations, so that the stranded carp can be revived early. Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Association.

Shanghai Municipal Council Regulations for Driving Signals 182

The Public Concession of the Shanghai Municipal Council, in order to manage traffic administration, has slightly modified the previous traffic regulations. The driving signals have also been approved and regulated by the Council. All drivers must use them to notify other drivers and patrolling police officers. The signals are recorded as follows: 1) "I am going to stop": Raise the stone arm straight up, or extend it horizontally to the right, and wave it up and down. 2) "I am going to turn right": Extend the right arm to the right. 3) "I am going to turn left": Extend the right arm to the right, then wave it across the body to the left. 4) "I am going forward": Extend the arm forward. 5) "You can go," "You can pass": Extend the right arm to the right, and wave the palm forward. If the driver's position on a motorcycle is on the left side of the vehicle, all the same signals must be indicated with the left arm. (Drivers may also use a mechanical or electrical device to emit any of the above signals, but its style must be approved by the Police Department. The installation of this device must not protrude beyond the overall width of the vehicle.)

Baoshan 183

Precautions After Repeated Robberies ▲Joint Meeting Held Yesterday

▲Police and Local Militia Implement Joint Defense ▲Inspection of Stations and Wharves

On the night before last, at around 8 PM, more than ten bandits armed with guns and electric torches suddenly arrived in Luodian Northwest Township, which is under the jurisdiction of Baoshan County. They robbed six or seven peasant households in the village before fleeing with shouts, resulting in a loss of approximately 600 yuan. Unexpectedly, around 10:30 PM, the residences of the Xu and Wang families in Dachang and Liuhang were robbed by bandits one after another. By the time the police and local militia arrived, the bandits had already fled far away. Yesterday, after receiving the report, Qiu Mingjiu, the county magistrate of Baoshan County, was extremely angry that robberies had repeatedly occurred in various townships under the county's jurisdiction, which seriously hindered local public security. He immediately convened a temporary joint meeting at around 2 PM yesterday afternoon, gathering the leaders of the first, second, third, and fourth public security bureaus, as well as the local militia, various agencies, and public organizations. The meeting was chaired by County Magistrate Qiu, and it was resolved: 1) Starting immediately, the police and local militia will implement joint defense to strengthen their forces. 2) Double posts will be added to all important sections, and special patrols will be assigned to remote areas. 3) At the Yanghang, Dachang, Liuhang, Luodian, and other bus stations, as well as the inland river docks, anyone getting on or off who is deemed suspicious must be inspected. If they are carrying packages, they must be opened and inspected. 4) Public places such as hotels and tea houses will be inspected to prevent bandits from hiding there. 5) Suspicious households and boats will be checked to prevent bandits from mixing in.

House Tickets Must Be Stamped 185

▲Proclamation of the French Concession Public Bureau

The Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court yesterday issued a proclamation stating that, for the matter of the proclamation, it was approved by the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance in Shanghai Special District Stamp Tax Office, stating that, according to the report from Liu Chuntuan and Shen Rulin, the stamp tax commissioners of the French Concession, it was recently read in the newspapers that the Special District Local Court announced that any house tickets in rent arrears litigation cases that are not stamped will be punished according to regulations. The French Concession should follow the same rule. It is proposed to request the French Public Bureau for assistance in following the precedent that, in future property litigation cases, any house tickets that are not stamped should be punished according to regulations, ordered to be stamped, and announced in advance so that everyone knows. Since its establishment, this office has written to the Public Bureau for assistance in promoting stamp sales as much as possible, so that it can proceed smoothly and increase tax revenue. The office is very grateful. House tickets should be stamped according to regulations. Currently, many property owners in the French Concession are complying with the regulations, but there are also many who have delayed complying. According to the aforementioned report, in addition to instructing the commissioners to provide earnest guidance at any time, the Public Bureau should be informed to investigate that, in future rent arrears litigation cases, any house tickets that are not stamped should be punished according to regulations, ordered to be stamped, and an announcement should be issued so that the public is aware. Please also order a copy of the draft to be sent to the office for publication in the newspaper. With utmost anticipation, etc. In addition to copying the draft and responding, the litigants are required to stamp house tickets in all rent arrears litigation cases from the date of this proclamation. If any have not been stamped, in addition to being ordered to be stamped, they will be punished according to regulations. Everyone must comply and not violate this proclamation, June 18th, 1931.

Children's Hygiene Movement 187

▲Lantern Parade Postponed to Tonight

The Chinese Child Welfare Association is organizing a children's hygiene movement. The lantern parade, originally scheduled for yesterday, was postponed to tonight due to the rain all day yesterday. Here is the information received yesterday: ▲Lantern Parade: Yesterday (the 18th) afternoon at 6 PM was the day for the lantern parade for the children's hygiene movement. However, due to the bad weather and rain all day, the parade could not be carried out. It was decided to postpone it to tonight. Children and boy scouts from various schools will gather in the field at the end of Qiujiang Road in Zhabei and depart in classes with lanterns at 6 PM. ▲Fly-Catching Competition: In the summer season, the most significant vector for infectious diseases is flies. Flies reproduce very quickly. As the weather has warmed recently, it is appropriate to reduce them through catching in a timely manner. The Association will hold a fly-catching competition for one week, divided into school and individual groups. The Association will send fly swatters and bags to municipal schools, and the schools will distribute them to the children to catch flies. Individuals can also participate. After one week, the Association will view the results of the catching, produce forms, and announce the results. The winners will be awarded prizes by the Association. The school group will be awarded banners, etc., for first, second, and third prizes. The individual group will be awarded ten prizes.

▲Free Injections: During the four days of the children's hygiene movement, doctors and nurses from the Municipal Health Bureau and the Public Concession Health Department will be dispatched to the Zhabei and Yangshupu Child Welfare Health Hospitals to give children visiting the exhibition area injections to prevent epidemics. ▲Lectures and Performances: Tonight, during the children's lantern parade, when all the teams have gathered, key members of the Association and representatives from the Education Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Health Bureau, etc., will give speeches on various issues of children's hygiene. Representatives from the Child Welfare Education Institute and the Youth Propaganda Team will then give performances. Afterward, a children's hygiene film will be shown in the area. ▲Children's Bathing: Today from 2 PM to 5 PM, children viewing the various children's displays at the Child Welfare Health Hospital on Qiujiang Road in Zhabei can declare their intention to take a bath at the hospital and join in order without paying a bathing fee. ▲Declaration of the Movement: Alas, our elders, brothers, sisters, uncles, and aunts! Have you heard the report from the Shanghai Pushan Manor? According to Pushan Manor's statistics, Shanghai averages one hundred coffined children's corpses collected every day. Calculated in this way, excluding those buried by families themselves, 36,000 young compatriots die every year. Is that not terrible? The reason for this is that people do not pay attention to hygiene, which makes it easy to spread diseases, leading to death. Although there are charity hospitals everywhere that can treat diseases, "knives and medicine are effective, but it is better not to cut," and "medicine is good, but it is better not to get sick." To avoid getting sick or being infected, hygiene is essential. However, there are also difficulties in this. For example, poor friends live in small, low houses, eat leftover tea and rice, and do extremely hard work. How can they pay attention to hygiene? What people do not know is that these poor friends need to pay even more attention to hygiene, because they live in small rooms with poor air quality, which makes them susceptible to disease. They eat leftover tea and rice that have been visited by flies and sleep in open-air places where mosquitoes bite, which makes them susceptible to infectious diseases. Once they get sick, they spread confusion everywhere. Children do not develop fully, and once infected, they are bound to die young. Therefore, this association has launched this children's hygiene movement! In particular, in the Zhabei area, there are the most friends doing small businesses, and in the Yangshupu area, there are the most friends doing labor. These friends in both places go out to seek food and clothing and neglect their children, letting them live and die on their own. Now that the weather is gradually getting hotter, and diseases will slowly come. If people do not pay attention to hygiene, and once epidemics become prevalent and diseases spread, it will be beyond redemption. Therefore, this association has launched the children's hygiene movement, which will be held first in the Zhabei and Yangshupu areas. This time, the event is larger than last year. In addition to requesting guidance from the government agencies, Social, Health, Public Security, Education, and Public Utilities Bureaus, many enthusiastic public welfare schools and organizations are participating and assisting. Although this movement of the association is said to be for children's hygiene, it is actually to urge parents to take responsibility, because children's happiness depends on adults seeking it for them. Naturally, children's health should also be sought by adults. This is a win-win situation: children's health and freedom from pain are the greatest happiness for the whole family. Being able to teach children about hygiene means that they themselves must understand hygiene. Therefore, this solemn declaration is made, hoping that our elders, brothers, sisters, uncles, and aunts will join and assist in making the local people have a common understanding of hygiene, so that the mortality rate of children can be reduced, and the number of healthy citizens in society can be increased. Then the children will be fortunate, the country will be fortunate, and the people will be fortunate.

Additional Four Cents per Dollar Added to Silk and Satin Dyeing Prices 189

Various silk and satin dyeing workshops in this city, due to the soaring prices of dyes and the sharp increase in coal prices, which have greatly increased costs, previously notified various silk businesses in January of this year of a four-cent surcharge per dollar. Now that the first accounting period of this year has arrived, the Shanghai Silk and Satin Dyeing Trade Association has sent separate letters to the Silk and Satin Trade Association, the Electrical Silk Weaving Trade Association, and the Xu Lun, Qianjiang, Crepe, and Shengjing guilds, stating: “Regarding the steadily rising prices of dyes and coal, your respective firms are well aware of this. Our industry has settled the dyeing accounts for the first period of the 20th year [of the Republic], and after deliberation at a general meeting, it was decided to increase the prices by 40% according to the regulations in the letters sent to various silk firms in January of this year (i.e., four cents per dollar). In addition to publishing a notice in the newspaper and informing the dyeing factories to comply, we are sending this letter accordingly. We respectfully request that you examine this, inform your respective silk firms, grant understanding, pay the full amount, and refrain from making difficulties. Post-holiday prices will be discussed and determined at a later date.”

Han and Xiao’s Housing Dispute Case Adjudicated 190

Han Boping previously sued Zhou Xiaozi Zhen over a dispute concerning jointly rented housing at the Public Concession Court. The court ordered Xiao to compensate the plaintiff, Han Boping, with a surplus of several thousand dollars. However, Xiao was dissatisfied with the judgment and hired a lawyer to file a false accusation, requesting a retrial. His request was granted, and after investigation, the debate was declared closed, awaiting a verdict. Yesterday, the date of the verdict arrived, and both parties were summoned to court. Judge Zhu ruled as follows: (Main text: The original judgment is revoked, and the defendant’s initial lawsuit in the retrial is rejected. The litigation costs are to be borne by the defendant in the retrial.) Reasoning: According to the plaintiff in the retrial, in 1925, he and the defendant in the retrial jointly leased a house in Huaqing Lane, Zhengjia Wood Bridge. Less than two months later, the defendant in the retrial moved to another place, which is an undisputed fact. This kind of joint lease of housing is not comparable to a separate business partnership. If the defendant in the retrial did not express any intention to dissolve the partnership or abandon the leasing fee when he moved out, then why did he neither transfer the lease to someone else at that time nor ask the plaintiff for the leasing fee? Now, after six or seven years, he has begun to negotiate and demand surplus rent. Furthermore, after the defendant in the retrial moved out, the plaintiff in the retrial bore the full rent. Later, because he did not want to continue living there, he terminated the lease in 1927, and Yang Xiao rented it instead. Regarding this point, the landlord's agent of the Sino-French Bank has provided proof, which further shows that the two parties no longer had a leasing relationship with the house. What disputes could there still be? The defendant in the retrial, in the initial trial, was in the position of the plaintiff and had the burden of proof. He neither presented any written agreement entered into with the plaintiff in the retrial nor proved who was subletting for profit and where the surplus was. These were just empty claims. The initial trial did not investigate carefully and hastily ordered compensation, which was quite inappropriate. Now, the plaintiff in the retrial's request for a retrial cannot be said to be unreasonable. Based on the above arguments, the retrial in this case is considered to be reasonable, and the judgment is made as stated in the main text.

▲Xu Shiying and Zhang Qun Officiated at the Wedding ▲Wang Xiaolai Delivered a Congratulatory Speech Minister of Communications Wang Boqun and Miss Bao Zhining, a graduate of Datong University, held their wedding ceremony at the Xu Garden on Connaught Road at 5:00 PM yesterday. Congratulatory guests filled the venue, and carriages clogged the streets, creating a grand scene for a time. The officiators were Xu Shiying and Zhang Qun, the introducers were Zhang Wenhua and He Jiwu, and the representatives of the parents were Mrs. Wang and Bao Junhao. The guests included Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Li Zhonggong, Cai Ziping, He Yaozu, Zhuang Zhihuan, Xu Xiuzhi, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Xizeng, and hundreds of colleagues from the Ministry of Communications, as well as dozens of foreign guests. Mr. Wang wore a blue robe and black mandarin jacket, while Miss Bao wore a white satin embroidered gown and a long veil, with an elegant demeanor, dignified and beautiful, and a beaming smile. After the ceremony, the officiator Xu Shiying delivered a congratulatory speech, saying, "Today, Mr. Boqun and Miss Zhining are holding their wedding ceremony. Mr. Boqun has devoted himself to the Party and the country and is in charge of communications. Therefore, I have an analogy. I am not good at rhetoric, so how dare I show off my skills in front of an expert? I hereby represent the guests in requesting Miss Bao to report on the process of their love." The crowd applauded and urged her to speak, but the master of ceremonies saw the opportunity and shouted to play music. Thus, the newly married couple exited the hall to the sound of music. Wang Bao and Li Ying's Photograph (Taken by this Newspaper) 203

This Newspaper's Photographic News Agency Takes Pictures 204

Scenery of the Three Gorges in Sichuan. The scenery of the Three Gorges where Sichuan and Hubei meet is magnificent, with precipitous cliffs, crumbling cliffs, and chaotic rocks, which are shocking to the eye. It is famous all over the world and is the only way for the Yangtze River to enter Sichuan. For thousands of years, due to the swiftness of the river and the treacherous shoals everywhere, it has been heard that civilian boats have hit reefs and had accidents every day. During the winter when the water is shallow, even steamers going upstream are often dangerous. Therefore, although the scenery has always been beautiful, few photographs have been circulated, because travelers are always wary, and the photographs taken by steamers passing by rarely achieve good results. This newspaper specially sent its Sichuan border photography reporters Wang Xiaoting and Liu Shuofu, who recently arrived in Chongqing from the Sichuan border. In view of this, they were willing to brave the dangers and travel down the river in a small boat, taking pictures along the way. Mr. He Beiheng, the director of the Sichuan River Shipping Department, greatly supported this initiative and specially ordered protection along the way and specially invited Mr. Leng Bofu, the owner of the Deyuan Photo Studio in Chongqing, to accompany them, specifically to take pictures of the dangerous shoals for the Shipping Department. It is learned that the three gentlemen took the Fushun ship to Fengjie on the 9th of this month, hired a small boat, and started from Kuifu, passing through Baidicheng, Kuimen, 灔澦堆, Qutang Gorge, Chijia, Baiyan, Ershan, Fengxiang Gorge, Wushan, Gaotang Temple, Shennu Temple, Wuxia, Twelve Peaks, Badong County, Zigui County, Quyuan Temple, Bingshu Baojian Gorge, Kongling Gorge, Niugan Mafei Gorge, Baigou Gorge, Huangniu Gorge, Dengyingzi Gorge (i.e., Xiling Gorge), and arriving at Yichang. The boat traveled in the river, taking pictures along the bank everywhere. Regardless of the precarious cliffs and dangerous rocks, they only sought a superior position and were not afraid to climb. When passing through Bashu, because the local area strictly guarded against the communists, a misunderstanding occurred with the local militia, and the militiamen fired guns, piercing two holes in the boat and shattering a tripod and three teacups. Fortunately, no one was injured. The films taken by the two gentlemen this time are mostly scenes that are not easily seen and will be gradually published in this newspaper's pictorial. According to the Wang Liu Er jun, who traveled west for more than half a month, they should be able to return to Shanghai tomorrow or the day after.
