The One Who Jumped to His Death 206

Turned Out to Be a Kidnapped Hostage ▲Was an Accountant at Ruikang Paint Store ▲Had No Contact After Being Kidnapped The case of an unnamed man jumping from the third floor at No. 2, Sicheng Lane, Julai Da Road, in the French Concession the day before yesterday, resulting in his immediate death, was reported in this newspaper. However, since the case occurred, people have been discussing it and have been unable to agree. However, according to the speculation of most people, it was said that he was mostly a kidnapped hostage, imprisoned there, and took the opportunity to jump from the building to escape, resulting in his unfortunate injury and death. It was not until the next day that someone came forward to claim the body. The deceased was indeed a local kidnapped hostage. At that time, Baldi, the Western detective of the French police, feared that the news would spread and make it difficult to solve the case, so he specially instructed the newspapers to postpone the disclosure. However, yesterday, the local news column of a certain newspaper had already described it in detail. This newspaper specially supplements the information to make up for the deficiency.

▲Often Did Not Return at Night It was found that the deceased's name was Wu Tingfang, from Ningbo, 44 years old, residing at No. 2 Junyi Lane, Belle Road, French Concession. He was currently the chief accountant at the Ruikang Paint Store on Wangping Street. In addition to his wife, Mrs. Liu, there was only a chauffeur and a maid at home. Wu took a car to the store every day around 9:00 AM, but Wu was extremely fond of gambling and often returned home late at night or did not return at all. ▲Suddenly Heard of the Kidnapping On the 26th of last month, Wu left home in the morning and did not return all night. At that time, his family only thought that Wu was out performing local opera and did not expect him to fall into the hands of bandits. Several days later, they suddenly received a letter from the bandits, urging them to pay a ransom. However, the letter did not specify the contact location or the amount of the ransom, so Wu's wife ignored it. Until the day before yesterday, Wu took advantage of the bandits' carelessness and jumped from the building to his death. ▲Indeed Identified Correctly Although Wu was over forty, he still had no children, so he adopted his nephew, Xiaojin, as his heir. The nephew, 25 years old, originally lived in Wenzhou and is now working at the Xiehe Kerosene Company in Tunchi, Anhui. He took leave a month ago to return home, and passed through Shanghai, staying at Wu's place. Yesterday, after reading the newspaper and observing the clothing, he was certain that it was his uncle. He told his mother, and they went to the morgue together to claim the body. Sure enough, it was Wu's body. The aunt and nephew were overwhelmed with grief and immediately gathered the family to move the body to the Siming Guild Hall. The body was placed in a coffin yesterday morning. After the funeral affairs are completed, the coffin will be taken back to their hometown for burial.

Kidnapper Ringleader 207

Continuation of the Trial of Shuai Songping ▲ Numerous witnesses give conclusive testimonies ▲ The Shuai household's furnishings are like those of the wealthy ▲ Shuai claims his family has a scholarly lineage for generations ▲ The current affair is a case of malicious fabrication Shuai Songping, also known as Shuai He, Shuai Huzi, Cai Songling, Cai Henian, Cai Peng, a native of Jiangxi who previously held prominent official positions, came to Shanghai after leaving politics and engaged in kidnapping. He acquired cars, motorcycles, and exquisite houses and equipment for kidnapping purposes. His operation was large-scale and could be considered the chief of kidnappers in Shanghai. On December 18th of last year, Lu Shaotang, a Suzhou native and comprador of the Compagnie Franco-Chinoise, was kidnapped by bandits on Yunnan Road. Lu's Russian bodyguard, Martis Tado, was shot and killed by the bandits. Less than half a month after the incident, Chief Inspector Lu Liankui of the General Inspectorate of the General Police Station, along with Inspectors Liu Shaokui, Tang Jian, Detectives Feng Zhiming, Wang Chengying, Detective Bao Wu Hanzhang, and others, uncovered the bandit den at No. 374 Hart Road, rescued the hostage Lu Shaotang, and arrested the kidnapper Hu Mingde, who was guarding the hostage. Four pistols and over a hundred bullets were seized.

Subsequently, the kidnappers Wang Sanhuai, Tian Changsan, and Liu Dianqing were apprehended and handed over to the Special District Court. They all confessed that the principal offender in the case was Shuai Songping. The Special Court later sentenced Wang and Tian to death, and Hu and Liu to life imprisonment. Meanwhile, an order was issued to all police stations to strictly apprehend Shuai and bring him to justice for interrogation. On May 2nd of this year, Shuai was suddenly arrested by the Beijing Municipal Public Security Bureau. Chief Inspector Lu ordered Inspector Liu Shaokui to bring Shuai to Shanghai and hand him over to the Special Court for interrogation and detention, as already reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xu Jiashi of the Criminal Court opened the first court to continue the trial. Shuai Songping hired lawyer E Sen to defend him. Lawyer Ru Baoyi of the police station stated that the police were prosecuting Shuai Songping under Article 2 of the Regulations for the Punishment of Kidnappers, Article 1 of the Regulations for the Prohibition of Military Firearms, and Item 1 of Article 284 of the Criminal Law. It was also stated that when Lu Shaotang was kidnapped, a motorcycle slowly preceded Lu's car, blocking it. The police later found that the vehicle was a Victory brand, number 238. Subsequently, the vehicle was discovered on Jiujiang Road and seized by detectives. Wang Sanhuai, who was driving the vehicle, was arrested. Wang confessed that the operation was based in room 51 of the Dadong Hotel, and the hostage was hidden in Shuai Songping's home at No. 414 Lane Lafei, Lafei Road. Detectives went to Dadong and apprehended Tian Changshan. They went to the Shuai's house but they did not find the kidnappers or the hostage. Later, under the guidance of the criminal Wang, they went to another residence of Shuai's at No. 374 Hart Road, where the hostage was rescued. The doorkeeper of Lane Lafei, Dai Shikui, also found a pistol in Shuai's garden, along with many bullets.

After the police arrested Shuai, they presented Wang Sanhuai and Tian Changshan. Wang and Tian identified Shuai from among the other criminals, stating that Shuai looked much thinner than before. Zhan Chengxiang, the rent collector for the house at No. 374 Hart Road, and Li Zhaokun, the driver, also testified that the keys to the house were given to Shuai, and the rent was also collected from Shuai. Cao Linbao, a tea server at the Dadong Hotel, also testified that Shuai frequently visited room 51. One of the four pistols seized from the Hart Road residence was examined by the Western detective Milers of the Bureau of Public Works, who determined that it was used to kill Tado. All the witnesses were present in court and available for questioning. Dai Shikui testified that he found a pistol inside the bamboo fence opposite Shuai's house. Western Detective Milers testified that one of the pistols seized from No. 374 Hart Road, with the number 629612, was the one used to kill Tado. Zhan Chengxiang testified that in June of last year, a young man came to the house of the landlord Cheng Zhongshi to rent the house. He claimed to be from Anhui, and his father was named Wang Zhisan, who had served in politics and was now in Shanghai to avoid the chaos. He paid a deposit of 20 yuan. The next day, Cheng asked me to visit Wang Zhisan at room 307 of the Dahua Hotel to discuss the rental procedures. I went and met the defendant, who claimed to be Wang Zhisan. I gave him the lease to find a guarantor. The defendant said that he was not familiar with Shanghai and could not find a guarantor from a shop, only a personal guarantor. He paid me the remaining rent of 110 yuan. In July, he moved in. In August, I went to collect the rent. The defendant gave me the lease with the name Wang Sanhuai as the guarantor. After the defendant and others moved in, I went to see the inside, and the furnishings were well-arranged and extremely luxurious, appearing like those of the wealthy, so I did not suspect anything. When I saw the defendant, he was a little fatter than he is now, etc. Li Zhaokun testified that he gave the house keys to Shuai and showed him the inside once. Cao Linbao testified that Shuai frequently visited room 51 of the Dadong Hotel. Wang Sanhuai and Tian Changshan, who had been sentenced to death, testified that the defendant was indeed Shuai Songping. When they went to kidnap Lu Shaotang, Shuai was still in room 35 of the Dadong Hotel. However, Shuai is now thinner than before, and his beard is also white. Hu Mingde and Liu Dianqing, who had been sentenced to life imprisonment, said they did not know Shuai Songping. At this point, the witnesses had finished their testimonies. Shuai Songping was then questioned, and Shuai firmly denied the charges, saying that he was in Tianjin at the time of the incident and that he was being falsely accused. He also stated that his family had a scholarly lineage for generations, his ancestor had served as the chief examiner of Shandong, and he was a civil servant, pleading for leniency. Judge Xu Jiashi verified the testimonies and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody, rescheduling the trial for July 3rd.

Chen Bingxiang Kidnapping Case 208

Suspicious Taxi Driver ▲ Car Once Carried a Bandit Away ▲ Taxi Also Used in Previous Kidnapping Case in Nanshi Cantonese Chen Bingxiang was kidnapped by bandits on Morrison Road the night before last. Fortunately, the taxi driver was alert and drove away quickly in an empty car. Although the bandits got the ransom, they could not return to the bandit den, so they all fled, allowing Chen to escape. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Afterwards, the Hongkou Police Station received a report from Wang Arong, a Tongzhou native and driver for the Zhongshan Taxi Company at No. 294 Zhaipu Road, which rented the car, stating that the bandit who rented the car claimed to be surnamed Qiu and rented the car to go to Baoxing Road, Zhabei, for business. After the incident, the man was still in the car and asked to be driven around the various roads for a week. When they reached Fujian Road, he paid a fare of 1.4 yuan and got out of the car. He appeared to have a pistol hidden in his sleeve. After investigation by Captain Mao Yiwen and Detective Liang Yongji, the police suspected that the driver, Wang Arong, was also involved in a case on the 12th of this month in Nanshi, where a person surnamed Mou was taken away in a car rented from the Zhongshan Company and driven by Wang Arong. Wang was brought back to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Special District Court, where he was interrogated by Judge Xiao.

The police lawyer stated that the kidnapped person shouted for help at the time and fled into the Japanese residence at No. 2. When the detectives arrived after hearing the alarm, the taxi driver was still carrying a bandit and did not stop the car. Furthermore, the taxi in the kidnapping case in Nanshi was also rented from the Zhongshan Company and driven by the same driver, making Wang highly suspicious. Wang Arong stated that he did not know that the person in the car was a kidnapper. The court ordered the defendant to be detained and further investigated.

Special Document

Fei Tang's Second Volume Report) Continued) 209

▲Abstract Translation of Parts Four and Five ▲Part Five This part describes the main issues regarding the future of the Public Concession. Chapter 1 lists the main issues that must be discussed according to the scope of Fei Tang's duties, tracing past facts. The motivation for the Public Concession to hire Fei was because a method would soon be adopted to "gradually abolish extraterritoriality in China," and they wanted Fei to make suggestions. However, it was clarified that the abolition of extraterritorial rights would have a significant impact on the entire status of the Public Concession. "However, the reason for preparing a construction plan for the future of the Public Concession is not only for the abolition of extraterritorial rights. Regardless of whether the abolition is near or far, the current system is peculiar in nature, and there are difficulties and dangers attached to the existing circumstances. Therefore, even if the status of extraterritorial rights does not change for the time being, all important issues must be addressed urgently." It then goes on to describe the widespread issues arising from the demand for "recovery." "Recovery" refers to "the termination of the existing system of the Public Concession and the return of its actual administration to Chinese management." The main issues regarding recovery are listed as follows: (1) The first is a general issue, namely, what are the reasons for supporting or opposing recovery? Whether the theory of those who support recovery, whether it is to be implemented immediately or ultimately, is convincing. It must be noted that the reasons put forward by those who advocate a policy of recovery are based half on theory and half on practice. In terms of theory, the existence of the current system of the Public Concession is an infringement of China's sovereignty. Therefore, returning the Public Concession to Chinese management is a legitimate and necessary step to satisfy the reasonable aspirations of the Chinese people. There are two points based on practice: (a) In some respects, the current administration of the Public Concession is imperfect and inefficient. If the concession is returned to Chinese management, these shortcomings can be remedied. (b) Whether the current administration of the Public Concession has been beneficial or culpable to those who actually reside or do business in the concession, dividing the entire Shanghai into three unconnected administrative regions, namely the Public Concession, the French Concession, and the Shanghai Municipal Government, results in a division of jurisdiction and significant disadvantages. Therefore, for the benefit of the entire Shanghai, its municipal system needs to be unified. The viability of the recovery claim, which is based on practice rather than theory, depends on further questions, namely (2) If recovery is implemented, what new system will replace the old system? If the existing governance regulations in the Land Regulations are about to disappear, will all local autonomy of the Public Concession be lost? Will the concession be merged with the adjacent Chinese area to be governed by a completely Chinese municipal system, without foreign participation? Or will a new system be established to maintain the existing system of autonomy and the cooperation between Chinese and foreigners in the existing local representative body? If the latter approach is adopted, will a representative municipal council be established in the Public Concession itself, or will it only be a part of the local autonomy organ organized for the entire Shanghai? In addition, there are important questions regarding timing: (3) If the principle of recovery is accepted, should recovery be an immediate goal, or should it be regarded as an ultimate goal? In other words, will the change be implemented immediately, or will it be implemented after a transitional period? (4) If a transitional period is required, how long should this period be, or what considerations should be used to determine the length of the transitional period? Then, it goes on to describe other key issues that need to be examined: (a) If the policy of recovery is not adopted, or (b) If recovery is deemed the ultimate goal of policy implementation, there must be a transitional period, during which the existing system of the Public Concession will remain unchanged. First, the issue of the relationship between the Public Concession and extraterritorial rights: In order to maintain the main characteristics of the Public Concession system, the most notable of which is to enable the municipal system established in accordance with the Land Regulations to continue, is it necessary to rely on the maintenance of extraterritorial rights, or at least to rely on the main countries in the concession to maintain their extraterritorial rights? Second, the existing governance system of the Public Concession needs to be reformed so that its shortcomings can be removed, or its nature can be improved. There are various issues regarding this reform. What are the current shortcomings and areas for reform regarding the following: (a) The organizational laws governing the organization and task methods of the taxpayer meeting and the organization and election methods of the board of directors? (b) The powers and responsibilities of the Bureau of Public Works in both administrative and legislative aspects within the Public Concession? (c) The powers that consuls and ministers of various countries may exercise over Public Concession affairs? (d) The relationship between the Bureau of Public Works and the central and local governments of China? (e) The exercise of judicial power by the courts in the Public Concession? ▲ Chapter 2 With reference to the above in this report, the Public Concession Bureau of Public Works is recognized as an executive body with administrative duties.

The current position and responsibilities of the Bureau are examined. The report indicates that although the Bureau is commonly known as the "Shanghai Public Concession Bureau of Public Works", in some respects its responsibility for governing is far greater than that of an ordinary municipal institution. The general situation regarding the scope of responsibility of the Bureau of Public Works and the magnitude of the interests it protects is outlined as follows: In addition to the ordinary responsibility of municipal management, the Bureau of Public Works must also be directly responsible for preventing internal and external troubles in order to maintain the safety of life and property within the Public Concession. The prosperity of Shanghai, and the welfare of Chinese and foreign residents in the Public Concession and its adjacent areas, clearly depend on the Bureau of Public Works fulfilling its responsibilities to the fullest extent. Since Shanghai is China's main commercial center, its importance means that the interests involved are far greater. If Shanghai cannot maintain law and order and sufficiently interfere with the credit and safe environment required for large-scale commerce, the economic impact will be far-reaching.

International and domestic trade, whether exported or imported, via the main rivers that converge in Shanghai, or directly or indirectly maintained and controlled by Chinese and foreign banks and commercial institutions in the Public Concession or its neighboring areas, will be stopped or hindered. Furthermore, the national government's tax revenue, collected from commerce passing through Shanghai or from industries centered in Shanghai, accounts for nearly half of the total customs revenue, and a large proportion of other taxes represented in the published budget. The amount of domestic government bonds raised by Chinese merchants in Shanghai is also far greater than elsewhere. Therefore, if riots or disturbances occur in Shanghai, depleting the important sources of tax revenue and government bonds, or significantly reducing the current large supply of funds from these sources, the government's finances will be exhausted. Among the issues affecting the future governance of the Public Concession, the interests that are involved and at risk are not only the interests of Chinese and foreign commercial firms and individuals engaged in industry and commerce within the Public Concession and the interests of their employees, but also general and far-reaching economic interests, including the interests of various parts of China with Shanghai as a commercial or banking center, the national interests of the entire China, and the interests of other countries, which vary according to the depth of their foreign trade relations with China. This is clearly obvious without further discussion. ▲ Chapter 3 Focuses on the attitude of Chinese and foreign residents in the Public Concession towards the issues affecting the future of the concession. The situation when Fei Tang arrived in Shanghai in January 1930 is described, with particular attention paid to "increasing the general approval" of the Chinese directors for various reasons, the most important of which is "that the atmosphere in January 1930, in terms of the relationship between Chinese and foreign residents in the concession, was better than two years earlier in dealing with issues affecting the future of the concession." The report then mentions how the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors from three to five, proposed in April 1930, was discussed. How the annual meeting of foreign taxpayers on April 16 rejected this proposal, and how the special meeting on May 2 passed this proposal with an absolute majority. The opinions expressed by leading Chinese and foreign merchants when talking to Fei Tang are excerpted in the report, and attention is paid to the fact that when quoting the opinions of "Chinese merchants", it is known that the merchants who express

This opinion is not only important, but it is truly related to businesses operated entirely by Chinese. It then mentions that the Chinese people insist on the demand to reclaim the concession, but it is clearly not an eagerness to reclaim it immediately. Responsible people in Chinese society are fully aware of the value of security provided by the concession system and do not want it to be changed easily. One of the facts that Chinese residents value is that "the Public Concession is able to govern itself without being controlled by the Chinese government or the Kuomintang because it enjoys the right of autonomy." Moreover, these Chinese people are well aware of how the Public Concession and the Chinese municipal territories connected to it differ in terms of autonomy. The opinions of the foreign community are described as follows: Leaders in the foreign community, while intending to acknowledge that China must eventually reclaim the Public Concession, also pay particular attention to the fact that it is not yet time to fundamentally change the status of the Public Concession. If any changes are made to its current status now, and the Public Concession is directly managed by the Chinese, there will be harm. These people clearly believe that security is an indispensable factor for the protection of commercial interests and the maintenance of Shanghai as a great industrial and commercial center. The meaning of security, as explained above, not only includes the protection of life and property from internal disturbances or external attacks, but also includes the maintenance of the rule of law in the Public Concession and exemption from illegal arbitrary taxes. They believe that this situation can only be achieved by continuing the governance system of the Bureau of Public Works while rejecting Chinese administrative officials from directly exercising their powers within the Public Concession. In other words, they want to maintain the Public Concession as a safe and well-governed urban area where residents can continue to enjoy the safety of life and property under the protection of the courts, and they firmly believe that if the Public Concession is returned to Chinese management now, there will be no hope of obtaining the above elements. Therefore, what they advocate is nothing else but that if Shanghai's future is to remain a commercial center, it depends on maintaining security in the broad sense, as described above. The attitudes of both Chinese and foreign residents are summarized by two slogans: What are these two slogans? They represent what people on both sides often say: "security" and "cooperation." "Security" is the slogan of the foreign community, because foreigners believe that unless the Public Concession continues to be governed by a board of directors with a majority of foreign representatives for a long time to come, its security cannot be maintained. Responsible Chinese merchants, although expressing this less directly, seem to recognize the necessity of security. And I can say that the majority of responsible Chinese merchants are prepared to agree that before China's situation becomes what they call "more stable", there is no hope of returning the Public Concession to Chinese management and having it provide the same security as the existing system of the Public Concession. In early 1930, and thereafter, I had private conversations with responsible Chinese and foreign business leaders, and based on the attitudes generally expressed by these leaders, I came to the conclusion that under the current circumstances, if it is certain that the various foreign countries intend to withdraw their troops stationed in China, and that in the near future, the Public Concession will be returned, and the conditions they set will make the Public Concession governed by the Chinese without restrictions, then an atmosphere of terror will fill the air, the foundation of credit will be greatly shaken,

Commerce will be stalled, and serious dangers will follow in the economic sphere. The Chinese slogan is "cooperation." Cooperation means that in the near future, the system of the Public Concession should be maintained jointly with foreigners, and the affairs of the Bureau of Public Works should be handled jointly with foreigners in a practical manner.

From the Chinese perspective, this will enable the administration of the Bureau of Public Works to take on a new look. The Chinese believe that in this way, the Bureau of Public Works will no longer be seen as an institution that maintains the power of foreigners to rule the Chinese, but will become an institution where Chinese and foreigners can jointly handle concession affairs to protect the common interests of all residents and promote the welfare of the Chinese and foreign communities. The sincerity of the Chinese people is demonstrated by how they nominated several prominent figures to serve as Chinese directors, and how these directors performed their duties. As for the foreign community, look at their acceptance of Chinese directors and the policies they adopted on issues that particularly affect the interests of the Chinese people. This not only shows that they have accepted the principle of cooperation, but also shows that they intend to put this principle into practice. In my opinion, as far as the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors is concerned, it is clear that not only the leaders of the foreign community have recognized that the cooperative efforts of Chinese and foreign residents are a necessary condition for the continuation of the concession system and the security it provides, but also the majority of the foreign community has recognized this. The above conclusion regarding the opinions of responsible Chinese merchants is based on private conversations. The statements of various Chinese groups quoted in Part Four, on the whole, do not contradict this conclusion. The statements naturally endorse the recovery of the concession, but there is a clear indication that there must be a transitional period before recovery. Even those who express the demand for immediate recovery are only making a formal proposal, because those who drafted the statements all hope for an extremely long transitional period, so that various organizational reforms and other innovations can be implemented in the concession during this period. It should also be remembered that the current situation in China often shows a consensus on certain issues, but this is only true on the surface and can be misleading. Because on this issue, it would be dangerous for Chinese people to express an opinion and openly oppose the demands that the masses often shout. Therefore, it is difficult for any Chinese person to express an opinion about the future of the concession publicly or semi-publicly, and it is difficult to publicly disagree with the demand for immediate recovery, even if it is to share the responsibility for expressing this opinion. Even if they express support for this demand in public, their individual opinion is completely opposed. ▲ Acknowledgement We thank the Commercial Press for donating Volume 28, No. 5 of the Eastern Miscellany, Volume 17, Nos. 4 and 5 of the Women's Magazine, and Volume 22, No. 3 of the Fiction Monthly, one copy each. Thank you. ▲ Correction Regarding the trademark rights of Old Beauty and Comet cigars, the American Tobacco Company is currently initiating legal proceedings, so the Belgian company Yinqinna has not obtained the above two trademarks.

Letter

To the Editor, After reading your newspaper report about the incident on the evening of June 1st, where bandits injured military police patrolling near the Zhengui Railway Station, there are many inaccuracies. According to the statement from the First Regiment of Military Police, on the evening of June 1st, the night fog was dense and visibility was near zero. Military police patrolling the area traveled to a location about three miles west of the Zhengui Railway Station when bandits suddenly opened fire, wounding two military police officers. During the chase, a speeding train passed by, separating us from the bandits, allowing them to escape. A search was conducted for a long time, but nothing was found. There was no arrest of foreign bandits. Most of the reports in the newspapers afterwards were not factual, especially the report of the arrest of foreign bandits, which is easily misunderstood. We are issuing this solemn statement to clarify the truth. We respectfully request that your newspaper correct this report to clarify the truth. Sincerely, Songhu Garrison Headquarters, June 18th.

Youth Corner

The Great Xia Wanbai Literary Society's Farewell to Graduating Members 211

— Zhong Heng

The Wanbai Literary Society of Great Xia University, known for its prestigious reputation, has seen its affairs flourish since the re-election this semester. It is heard that with the summer vacation approaching, more than ten of its members are about to graduate. In order to bid farewell to the graduating members and report on the society's affairs, the society held a farewell party for the graduating members at the Great Xia Hotel the day before yesterday. More than fifty people attended. At seven o'clock, the society's chairman, Mr. Tong Shiquan, presided over the meeting, with Mr. Gao Liepeng serving as the recorder. First, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating that today's meeting is a farewell party for the graduating members, and there are four purposes that can be reported. The first is that at the end of the semester, the society's affairs should be gathered with all members to make a detailed report. The second is that some members of the society will graduate from the school this semester. Everyone has been like-minded and has been together for a long time. Once separated, whether serving society or studying abroad, they will be separated by distance and see each other less and less. The psychology of parting is common to all, so there must be today's meeting to commemorate us. The third is that the graduating gentlemen have specialized knowledge, and will either dedicate themselves to society or continue their studies in the future. The society sincerely hopes that you will work hard for the country and seek happiness for society. The fourth is that we are busy all day long, and there are few opportunities to gather together, and in a wandering life, we are all guests in a strange land, and we still meet today when we are about to part. So we feel that today's gathering is worth commemorating. After the chairman finished his report, Mr. Wang Ruinian delivered a farewell speech on behalf of the society. In addition, Dr. Huang Jingsi, a member of the society, gave a speech, mainly on three points regarding the society and the graduating members: first, there must be a spirit of cooperation; second, there must be the courage to fight; and third, it must be organized. Finally, graduating members Zhang Zhenyong and Xu responded one after another, briefly stating that they were very grateful for your kindness, and that they would bravely move forward and work hard for the Party and the country, hoping to meet the society's expectations. Afterwards, various recreational performances were performed to add to the fun. Among them, Wang Yingjun's "The Unofficial Biography of Taizhen," Wu Zongrong's "Nanyang Pass," and Yi Kejian's "Fenhe Bay" all won a lot of cheers. Finally, the chairman told a very humorous joke and the meeting adjourned. The clock struck ten.
